        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544835995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4974127921570011194">What a peculiar little book... First of all, the blurb doesn't do it justice at all. It makes it sound like another silly romance-centered YA with nothing else to give than brooding love interests and never-ending eye descriptions, and that's so not what's happening here. <br/>It was almost a 4 stars read until the last 20% or so, where everything felt rushed and not developed enough to be credible. A real pity because I enjoyed the writing a lot - be warned though, the 3rd person present tense will </span>
  <span id="freeText4974127921570011194" style="display:none">What a peculiar little book... First of all, the blurb doesn't do it justice at all. It makes it sound like another silly romance-centered YA with nothing else to give than brooding love interests and never-ending eye descriptions, and that's so not what's happening here. <br />It was almost a 4 stars read until the last 20% or so, where everything felt rushed and not developed enough to be credible. A real pity because I enjoyed the writing a lot - be warned though, the 3rd person present tense will not appeal to all - and the ambiance was a success.<br /><br />It reminded me, in a way less horrific way, of Summer of Night by Dan Simmons, a beloved book of mine that I still adore even if it terrified me enough to fuck up my nights for a decade. <br />Rural america, small town setting, a very different way to live than the urban life we mostly know.<br />But where Dan Simmons wrote a very adult book, Lisa McMann stays in the YA realm. It's not a bad thing, except that the book could have been a killer with more development, more time to scatter details here and there and to wrap up the whole discovery/conclusion nicely. It's so rushed that it discredits the plot.<br /><br />One thing I really, really liked was that McMann chose to give her main character OCD and I think it's very well depicted here. It's not just mentioned like when authors try to but fail, it's entirely part of the story, part of who Kendall is and as it plays such a big part in her life, it plays a big part in how she's gonna handle the happening events.<br /><br />Many other topics are broached : being a non-white new guy in an almost all-white town, being a teenager in a small town when it's all you've ever known, being a teenager in a small town when you had to live the big city and another life behind, being a girl in a masculine environment, having your life shattered because suddenly the world is a bad place, and dealing with grief and guilt.<br /><br />A quick and interesting read that will have trouble to gain readers outside the YA audience because of its lack of development. Still very pleasant to read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4974127921570011194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120195323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120195323" />
    <a title="hayden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden"><img alt="hayden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598996671p2/2995566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120195323?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hayden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hayden" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden">hayden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=f-ckin-amazing">f-ckin-amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=history-with-author">history-with-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=ending-rocked">ending-rocked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=mega-awesome-cover">mega-awesome-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=i-heart-the-characters">i-heart-the-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=ss-galley-grab">ss-galley-grab</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120195323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13048422919941679706">If I could only use one word to describe this book (whether it be short, long, medium, descriptive, simple, or in-between), it'd simply be <b> terrifying. </b> Don't tell me you haven't gotten the horror vibes from this book! How creepy would it be to walk into school and find etchings like <b> TOUCH ME </b>, <b> ONLY YOU CAN SAVE ME </b>, and <b> SAVE MY SOUL </b> inscribed into your desk? I don't know about you, but I'd be absolutely, mind-blowingly horrified.<br/><br/>That's the feeling this book gives off. The horror aspect of t</span>
  <span id="freeText13048422919941679706" style="display:none">If I could only use one word to describe this book (whether it be short, long, medium, descriptive, simple, or in-between), it'd simply be <b> terrifying. </b> Don't tell me you haven't gotten the horror vibes from this book! How creepy would it be to walk into school and find etchings like <b> TOUCH ME </b>, <b> ONLY YOU CAN SAVE ME </b>, and <b> SAVE MY SOUL </b> inscribed into your desk? I don't know about you, but I'd be absolutely, mind-blowingly horrified.<br /><br />That's the feeling this book gives off. The horror aspect of the novel is illustrated gorgeously in your head. You feel like you can't turn pages fast enough to just get to the frickin' end and SEE WHAT HAPPENS ALREADY. The challenges OCD presents to Kendall and her friends is valid (other reviews have said it's completely falsified and shallow), but I know otherwise, because, for one, McMann's daughter has it, and I don't know an easier way to figure out how OCD works than to go to your daughter; and, for two, I have a mild, self-prescribed case of it as well. I mean, I don't have to face all of the difficult challenges Kendall does (uh, hence the "mild" part), nor do I feel trapped by it, but by all means I know what it's like to struggle with it.<br /><br />One thing about CRYER'S CROSS that makes me really happy (especially considering this is a horror novel, and I can point to specific horror novels that don't do this, or don't do it well) is how resolved the story is. I know exactly where the horrific aspect of the novel comes from, and I know what happens to the cause, which deeply satisfies me, more than an open-ended version would. I like knowing what/who/where did this, and I like how it's not left for me to try and make an informed decision about, left with a million branches, and I have to find the right one. I don't like when authors do this because the story feels horribly gypped and like the author didn't know enough about his/her own story to create a coherent ending. That being said, McMann didn't totally overcrowd our heads with information about the conclusion, just gave us enough info to where we're satisfied but there's still a little bit of an open ending as to what happened to the characters and the horror aspect.<br /><br />McMann is an extremely versatile author, being able to go from YA fantasy (THE UNWANTEDS, coming Sept '11) to this. I just now put her on the non-existent list of i-will-buy-anything-this-author-writes (which, you know, I really should make a shelf for).<br /><br /><br /><b> CRYER'S CROSS is a gripping tale with a perfect resolution that I couldn't get out of my head for days . . . fantastic and horrifying! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13048422919941679706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_144580882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144580882" />
    <a title="Milly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4000502-milly"><img alt="Milly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291008553p2/4000502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144580882?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milly" href="/user/show/4000502-milly">Milly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lisa McMann fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144580882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1705551474066023346">Cryer's Cross is the very first horror book I finished in a day! Usually, I get too scared to keep reading that I have to stop and put down the book, come back to it days later, and hopefully read a few chapters at a time. What can I say, I have a low tolerance for horror! I can't even pick up any books from Dean Koontz anymore since the last one I read of his gave me nightmares for days on. So, it was a relief to come across Cryer's Cross, which had just the right amount of horror for my taste.</span>
  <span id="freeText1705551474066023346" style="display:none">Cryer's Cross is the very first horror book I finished in a day! Usually, I get too scared to keep reading that I have to stop and put down the book, come back to it days later, and hopefully read a few chapters at a time. What can I say, I have a low tolerance for horror! I can't even pick up any books from Dean Koontz anymore since the last one I read of his gave me nightmares for days on. So, it was a relief to come across Cryer's Cross, which had just the right amount of horror for my taste. <br /><br />I almost did not pick up this book because of the so-so reviews from my peers but now I'm thankful that I took a chance and read another of Lisa McMann's. I really enjoyed her Wake series and definitely enjoyed Cryer's Cross. I was sucked into the story from the very beginning and I could not separate from the book thereafter, so curious to find out who the killer is! I know to some it was a disappointment in the end when the killer is revealed. To me, it was definitely creepy and reminiscent of all the horrific stories I was told growing up. They may sound out of this world to most people but to me, they are horrific and still nightmare-worthy. I have had one or two paranormal experiences growing up so having a villain as such in the story is actually not that overreaching, believe it or not. <br /><br />The other thing I liked about Cryer's Cross is that the plot is refreshing and unique, at least to me. I have not read a book with a similar plot and I appreciate that very much. Also, I loved the setting chosen for this book. The culture of Bozeman is quite interesting and intriguing especially as a result of its small community. I couldn't imagine sharing a classroom with the entire high school and know each and everyone there. It reminds me of the olden days when life was much simpler and people pretty much live off their land, just like in the book. Everyone knew each other and people actually rode horses to school and to town. I wouldn't mind living like that. Just reading about the beauty of Montana and the simplicity of it all was mesmerizing. It makes me want to visit the place and visualize the characters, the homes they live in, the school they go to, and the farms they tended. <br /><br />Kendall, the female protagonist of the book was definitely a unique character. This is the first time I've read about a character with OCD. She is quite interesting and realistic enough. I've worked with enough kids with OCD and I have seen first hand how the compulsion and the obsession could be so debilitating to these kids that they have to be medicated to manage them. It is nice to read about someone who's able to manage the disorder without medicating herself as in the case of Kendall. Intense gross motor activity definitely helps to curb some of the obsession and compulsion even for a short period of time just like we see with Kendall when she plays soccer. It was fascinating for sure to read about her different quirks and rituals. We all find ways to cope with stress and to find things we could control in our environment. Kendall was no different. She's no different from a hoarder, just perhaps more interesting and cleaner. It's ironic that her disorder becomes her saving grace in the end. <br /><br />As for the men in this book, I really didn't have a preference for either one. I liked Nico because he was a nice guy. He did everything right and was Kendall's rock for a long time. Jacian on the other hand was unpredictable, rough around the edges, and intriguing. Definitely not my preferred literary male character but either one was good enough to make Kendall swoon. <br /><br />I really enjoyed my time spent reading Cryer's Cross. Lisa McMann did not disappoint. It was gripping, refreshing, interesting, and entertaining. Overall, a solid 4 read!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1705551474066023346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130518344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3186603522539813393"><strong>Original post at <a href='http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/cryers-cross/' rel='nofollow noopener'>One More Page</a></strong><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>Cryer's Cross</strong>
</em> tells the story of Kendall Fletcher, a girl with OCD who lives in the small town of Cryer's Cross in Montana. It starts with the entire town searching for Tiffany Quinn, who disappeared without a trace shortly before Kendall's junior year ended. When the town eventually gives up on looking for her, everything sort of goes back to normal until Kendall's best friend and sort of boyfriend, Nico, also disappears. Kendall is distraught, until she finds </span>
  <span id="freeText3186603522539813393" style="display:none"><strong>Original post at <a href="http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/cryers-cross/" rel="nofollow noopener">One More Page</a></strong><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Cryer's Cross</strong>
</em> tells the story of Kendall Fletcher, a girl with OCD who lives in the small town of Cryer's Cross in Montana. It starts with the entire town searching for Tiffany Quinn, who disappeared without a trace shortly before Kendall's junior year ended. When the town eventually gives up on looking for her, everything sort of goes back to normal until Kendall's best friend and sort of boyfriend, Nico, also disappears. Kendall is distraught, until she finds something very peculiar: Nico and Tiffany sat in the same desk in school, and Nico seemed to be sending Kendall graffiti messages through this desk.<br /><br />Lisa McMann delivers again in this deliciously creepy novel about a small town with secrets through the eyes of a girl with OCD. It's almost similar with the Dreamcatcher series in terms of its sparse prose, and yet <strong>
  <em>Cryer's Cross</em>
</strong> has a more poetic feel about it with how the town was described and the people who live there. It had a somewhat initial similar feel to <a title="Once Was Lost" href="http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/once-was-lost" rel="nofollow noopener">Sara Zarr's <em>Once Was Lost</em></a>, but it got creepier and creepier especially after reading some of the messages from "WE" in between some chapters such as this one:<br /><blockquote>WE<br /><br />When it is over, We breathe and ache like old oak, like peeling birch. One of Our lost souls set free. We move, a chess piece in the dark room, cast-iron legs a centimeter at a time, crying out in silent carved graffiti. Calling to Our next victim, Our next savior. We carve on Our face:<br /><br /><strong>TOUCH ME.</strong></blockquote><br />It came to a point that I was too scared to read this book when I was traveling alone or when I'm the only one left awake at home, which was why it took me a while to read this book (I'm a big chicken, too bad). The book's pacing was slow at first, but the author takes this time to set it all up, building up to a very creepy climax.<br /><br />Perhaps my only gripe in this book is the reason why the things were happening felt a little...I don't know, abrupt? It was a perfectly creepy and horrifying reason, but it felt like it totally came from nowhere. Of course, this may be done on purpose to hike up the creepiness factor, although I kind of wish for a bit more foreshadowing on that piece of Cryer's Cross history.<br /><br />Nevertheless, this is another solid book for Lisa McMann. I can't wait to read what she comes up with next.</span>

<div id="review_137082603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137082603" />
    <a title="Hafsah Faizal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277009-hafsah-faizal"><img alt="Hafsah Faizal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530680722p2/4277009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137082603?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hafsah Faizal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hafsah Faizal" href="/user/show/4277009-hafsah-faizal">Hafsah Faizal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137082603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1298708707063167133"><a href='http://www.iceybooks.com/2011/01/cryers-cross-by-lisa-mcmann.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>See Review on Blog</b>
</a><br/><br/> Compelling and creepy, Cryer's Cross was one book I just couldn't put down, yet at the same time, I wanted to. It was haunting, and I made the mistake of reading it only hours before bed. And I have an old wooden desk, with scrapes and marks all over it, which only made things worse. <br/><br/> From the very first page, there's trouble. Tiffany Quinn is missing, and in the small town of only 212, one missing teen is a really big deal. After months of searching, they give up, and soo</span>
  <span id="freeText1298708707063167133" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.iceybooks.com/2011/01/cryers-cross-by-lisa-mcmann.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>See Review on Blog</b>
</a><br /><br /> Compelling and creepy, Cryer's Cross was one book I just couldn't put down, yet at the same time, I wanted to. It was haunting, and I made the mistake of reading it only hours before bed. And I have an old wooden desk, with scrapes and marks all over it, which only made things worse. <br /><br /> From the very first page, there's trouble. Tiffany Quinn is missing, and in the small town of only 212, one missing teen is a really big deal. After months of searching, they give up, and soon, life goes on as normal in the small farming city of Cryer's Cross. Then the new guy and his sister move in. Jacian is full of rage and Kendall can't help but imagine Jacian kidnapping Tiffany and cutting her up into uncountable pieces. <br /><br /> The tension builds, and between chapters, eerie messages of 'We' and 'Us' only add to the suspense. Though we don't learn much about the characters, I found myself needing to turn the next page, just to see what would happen. When Nico, Kendall's best friend, goes missing, Kendall's life breaks. She's drawn to his desk, the same desk Tiffany Quinn used last year, and she can't help think maybe she'll disappear if she uses it. Maybe disappearing won't be so bad.<br /><br /> But then come the voices, the whispers, the begging. Then everything changes. What Kendall first dismisses as impossible is actually possible and can't be ignored. In the small town of Cryer's Cross, Montana, something is happening. <br /><br /> I had mixed feelings at times. I didn't get to learn much about Kendall, though I like the fact that she's a normal teen, with an OCD problem. But the plot was enough to steer my review to five stars. Cryer's Cross was a quick read, and you'll find yourself sucked in before you know it. And by then, it'll be too late to pull yourself back out. Lisa McMann's latest novel is a thriller you just can't miss out on.<br /><br /> I love the cover. It's as haunting as the story itself. If I didn't know what the story was about, the cover would be enough for me to pick up the book. The desk in the dark room and the etched-on title hold a lot of significance to the story.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290204016" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5927169-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496236285p2/5927169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290204016?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/5927169-sofia">Sofia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290204016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3692828921118106554">Lisa McMann isn’t a new author for me. I’ve read and loved her Dream Catcher trilogy so when I got Cryer’s Cross, aka The Missing, I was very excited to jump into it.<br/><br/>In the small town of Cryer’s Cross nobody is safe anymore. After two teens are gone missing, the people of the town are shaken and especially Kendall Fletcher. When Kendall’s best friend/ boyfriend, Nico goes missing, she isn’t sure she can cope. Kendall has known Nico all of her life and she can’t remember even a moment when Nico w</span>
  <span id="freeText3692828921118106554" style="display:none">Lisa McMann isn’t a new author for me. I’ve read and loved her Dream Catcher trilogy so when I got Cryer’s Cross, aka The Missing, I was very excited to jump into it.<br /><br />In the small town of Cryer’s Cross nobody is safe anymore. After two teens are gone missing, the people of the town are shaken and especially Kendall Fletcher. When Kendall’s best friend/ boyfriend, Nico goes missing, she isn’t sure she can cope. Kendall has known Nico all of her life and she can’t remember even a moment when Nico wasn’t there to help her when she needed him. Now she’s alone, struggling to control her OCD and determined to find out what happened to her best friend. Everything gets complicated when a new family moves into the small town and the oldest son, Jasian is a suspect. <br /><br />I really loved this book. When I first started reading it I was very confused with the flow. The story is told in third person but there were times that we hear a mystery voice. I had no idea what was going on until the end. That was really creepy by the way.<br /><br />Kendall was so different from the average heroine. She had to struggle with her OCD in her everyday life and Nico had always been there to help her when things got tough. Now everything is changing. Her best friend is missing never to be found, her dreams of dancing are falling apart and as if that wasn’t enough she has to face Jasian, who isn’t the bad guy everyone though after all. She was so compassionate yet curious for the world around her. She never gave up on her search for Nico which was a sign for her inner strength while the guilt about accusing Jasian, consumed her.<br /><br />I also loved Jasian and his sister. Their start with Kendall wasn’t good but they were both there for her when she thought she had no one to rely on. Jasian was so mature for his age. He was supposed to be the bad guy in town but all he wanted was to fit in. His relationship with Kendall was complicated in the beginning but he never gave up on her.<br /><br />Cryer’s Cross, aka the missing, was a great YA horror/ romance with a lot of suspense and a long forgotten secret of a small town. I can’t believe I didn’t read it sooner.<br /><br />I highly recommended!<br /><br />Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sofialovesreading.blogspot.gr/2015/06/review-missing-by-lisa-mcmann.html">http://sofialovesreading.blogspot.gr/...</a></span>

<div id="review_156058084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156058084" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156058084?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156058084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10555424716236757481">First of all, I need to point out that this is NOT a dystopia. The reason I picked the book up was because I had seen it described thus somewhere, but it isn't. Cryer's Cross is actually more of a psychological thriller/fantasy/horror story. I wish it had been a dystopia.<br/><br/>Last year, I read Lisa McMann's Wake Trilogy, which I sort of liked at first, but later came to almost abhor. Her writing drove me crazy. It's so incredibly fragmented. Everyone told me that the writing was matched to Janie's th</span>
  <span id="freeText10555424716236757481" style="display:none">First of all, I need to point out that this is NOT a dystopia. The reason I picked the book up was because I had seen it described thus somewhere, but it isn't. Cryer's Cross is actually more of a psychological thriller/fantasy/horror story. I wish it had been a dystopia.<br /><br />Last year, I read Lisa McMann's Wake Trilogy, which I sort of liked at first, but later came to almost abhor. Her writing drove me crazy. It's so incredibly fragmented. Everyone told me that the writing was matched to Janie's thoughts and not a sign of McMann's inability to compose a complex sentence. Well, that excuse really does not fly here. The story is told in third person and yet, oddly enough, the syntax remains choppy and composed largely of sentence fragments. This will, hopefully, be my last foray into McMann.<br /><br />All that so grumpily said, Cryer's Cross was not a terrible read. I think I liked it more than I disliked it. The ending was a bit too mystical for my taste, but there was a major redeeming factor. The one thing McMann does really well: she writes really attractive, atypical male leads. And some pretty hot scenes with them, even if they remain PG, as is the case here.<br /><br />I recommend this for reluctant readers, although I doubt boys would be too interested. For a book with a lot of menace lingering about, there is very little action.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10555424716236757481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3068319936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3068319936" />
    <a title="Megaira With The Owls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104125593-megaira-with-the-owls"><img alt="Megaira With The Owls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575228923p2/104125593.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3068319936?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megaira With The Owls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megaira With The Owls" href="/user/show/104125593-megaira-with-the-owls">Megaira With The Owls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3068319936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13030527935011623494">How in the world does this book have such a high rating???<br/>Well, I will clearly be in the minority then.<br/><br/>I picked this book up from a skip that stood on the pavement near my house. I absolutely hate it when people just throw books away, so I thought I would save this one.<br/>Might have been a mistake.<br/><br/>The story follows a young girl, Kendall, whose classmates start disappearing. Whilst worrying about them and trying to find out what happened, she is fighting her own demons – she suffers from OCD and she</span>
  <span id="freeText13030527935011623494" style="display:none">How in the world does this book have such a high rating???<br />Well, I will clearly be in the minority then.<br /><br />I picked this book up from a skip that stood on the pavement near my house. I absolutely hate it when people just throw books away, so I thought I would save this one.<br />Might have been a mistake.<br /><br />The story follows a young girl, Kendall, whose classmates start disappearing. Whilst worrying about them and trying to find out what happened, she is fighting her own demons – she suffers from OCD and she is also getting increasingly influenced by the “villain” of the story. To complicate matters, there is also a new love interest in town.<br /><br />Now, the premise did sound really interesting. There was potential. Unfortunately, it was completely wasted. The only reason why I have given it 2 stars and not 1, is because the protagonist is actually quite likeable and relatable – so the book does evoke some positive feelings in the reader.<br />However, this is the only positive in this whole novel. Let me make a list of the things that were not so good, starting from the mild ones, and ending with the most serious one:<br /><br />1. Third person present tense narration. WHY???<br />I consider present tense such a cheap shot on the part of the thriller writers. It feels like they are trying to force the suspense on me and also trying to force this sense of rushing through the action. I always feel like I am chasing sentences, instead of savouring them. A good thriller does not need this, there are so many other ways to evoke suspense and introduce actual thrills. <br /><br />2. The “villain” / evil object. It is the most ridiculous thing ever. If you would like a spoiler, here is:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ An evil school desk. What.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3. The romance. I read the blurb and I went “Ooh, a thriller, sounds really good, I might enjoy this.” And then, about 60% of the story is a budding romance. Not what I signed up for!<br /><br />4. The tropest of the tropes – the love interest is a stand-offish jerk who then turns out not to be a jerk. Really? Star Wars has done it already, and has done it much better (not to mention the countless books and other movies that have done it, as well). Can we please not have the watered-down, school-jock versions of Han Solo in our thrillers?<br /><br />5. The worst one: presenting a mental disorder as beneficial. <br />This is difficult to discuss without spoiling, but I am going to try. At one point of the story, OCD is a factor that somehow (not quite sure how, it is a mystery) becomes a savior. Kendall says she is never going to complain about it again. <br />Excuse me? <br />I now suffer from a mild form of OCD. It used to be much worse. Let me give you one example: I would come back up the stairs to a 2nd-floor flat after leaving the building, sometimes 5, 7, 8 times, because I had to check over and over again if I had locked the door, turned the cooker off, closed the windows, not left the iron on. I would cry with frustration, I would know I would be late, and yet I would still do it, nonetheless. This is just one example. <br /><br />I am much better these days, but I feel flabbergasted that anyone could present this as beneficial in any way, shape or form. I just find it completely unrealistic. And that statement of Kendall’s where she is never going to “complain about it again” seems to be both trivialising and at the same time glorifying a disorder that can be an absolute nightmare for the affected. It made it sound like OCD was an issue on par with a runny nose that somehow helps fight villains (I don’t know how. Incapacitates villains by shooting boogers at them? Your suggestions are welcome.)<br /><br />All in all, I am very underwhelmed. I wish more time was spent on discovering the secrets of the town’s inhabitants, as this could have been much, much more interesting, especially coupled with all the difficulties a sleuth suffering from OCD might encounter. It could have gone in a much fresher, livelier direction.<br />This book left me feeling like it needed re-writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13030527935011623494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_601190116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601190116" />
    <a title="DrasticallyMild" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19393385-drasticallymild"><img alt="DrasticallyMild" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365894030p2/19393385.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601190116?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DrasticallyMild" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DrasticallyMild" href="/user/show/19393385-drasticallymild">DrasticallyMild</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19393385-drasticallymild?shelf=ash">ash</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601190116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15398184520192696195">Cryer’s Cross. It’s a book I picked up at the book story because it was in the bargain section and someone said it was “eerie, gripping” yadda yadda yadda. I’m not too sure why but I trusted this person, probably because I hadn’t read a good mystery/thriller in a while.<br/>	I should have known better. I should have seen through Cryer’s Cross’s (tee hee, that looks funny) guise. Somehow, absorbed in false hope, a book called Cryer’s Cross with a stupid looking desk on the cover got me to buy it. It t</span>
  <span id="freeText15398184520192696195" style="display:none">Cryer’s Cross. It’s a book I picked up at the book story because it was in the bargain section and someone said it was “eerie, gripping” yadda yadda yadda. I’m not too sure why but I trusted this person, probably because I hadn’t read a good mystery/thriller in a while.<br>	I should have known better. I should have seen through Cryer’s Cross’s (tee hee, that looks funny) guise. Somehow, absorbed in false hope, a book called Cryer’s Cross with a stupid looking desk on the cover got me to buy it. It took advantage of my sorry state and I had to pay the price.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/515752.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Now, on with the actual review. <br><br>I think there a five main subject/plotpoints/whatever you want to call them in this book. I’m going to touch upon each of them. In order because I’m just totally fly that way.<br><br><b>1 – A Girl with OCD</b><br>First, we have Kendall. She lives in a small town with her mum. And, said mum, is always asking Kendall, “How’s your OCD?” Sometimes, throughout the book Kendall’s OCD suddenly grips her and overpowers her. Towards the end of the novel it’s her OCD that saves her… somehow. <br>McMann has a daughter diagnosed with OCD and the character, Kendall, is based off of her. I think that the topic of and Kendall’s dealings with OCD could have been portrayed so much better. It’s such a large part of the story but I find that the way McMann introduced it and continued to represent it was not only slightly annoying but unrealistic. She persistently ‘told’ and didn’t show.<br>And honestly, do you ask you daughter how their OCD is “doing”? Yes? No? Maybe? I dunno? I don’t think so. If you think I’m wrong feel free to call me a stupid impudent child, tell me I have no idea what I talking about. But think about first. Really think about it.<br><br><b>2 – Missing People</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419241ra/830939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Two people go missing from the town Kendall lives in, one of them being Kendall’s boyfriend, Nico. The townspeople are mad and sad and it’s all very mysterious.<br><br><b>3 – An Evil Desk</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/571758.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The desk that is shown on the cover of the book is an evil one. That is unless you bought or read or have only seen an edition of the cover that doesn’t have a desk on it. As in, the desk isn’t shown on the cover, it’s still evil.<br>	Why is it evil you ask? Because it talks to you and makes you possessed and gets you ‘high’. I’m not kidding. McMann used the word ‘high’ to explain the feeling of ‘euphoria’ that Kendall felt when she touched some words on the desk and listened to a voice. That’s what happened.<br>	Lots of people said it was creepy and spooky and eerie and mysterious. You know what I say?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419241ra/830940.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4 – A ‘Sizzling’ Romance</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419241ra/830941.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A boy moves to town, Kendall questions her feeling for Nico, blah blah blah. It’s basically what the book is about but it’s just filler so there’s not all that much to it. Hence the short paragraph.<br><br><b>5 – Dirt and mud and rain</b><br>They play soccer in dirt and mud and rain. They walk in dirt and mud and rain. They get covered in dirt and mud and rain. And they get buried in dirt and mud and rain.<br><br><b>A couple more things:</b><br>McMann tells the story in third person present tense. It’s awful. First person would have, in my opinion, much better suited this novel We’d have gotten a clearer image of Kendall’s OCD and maybe I would have been able to feel some sort of emotion other than ‘annoyance at the author’.<br>Through some of the book there were these little pieces of text between paragraphs that were kind of cool.<br>If you haven’t gathered, I wasn’t impressed with this book.<br><br>The End.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15398184520192696195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_162959429" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162959429" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4002283-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352094603p2/4002283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162959429?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/4002283-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4002283-michelle?shelf=young-adult-luvin">young-adult-luvin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4002283-michelle?shelf=paranormal-and-supernatural-world">paranormal-and-supernatural-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4002283-michelle?shelf=ya-paranormal-fantasy-romance">ya-paranormal-fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4002283-michelle?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162959429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8084516572709046273">Holy crap. Ladies and gentlemen, Lisa McMann has done it once again. This book was similar to the Dream Catcher trilogy (Wake, Fade and Gone) yet so different. Cryer's Cross totally brought the words 'eerie' and 'haunting' to a whole new level, well maybe not, but its sure damn close! It had me shuddering throughout but I couldn't bring myself to tear away from the pages, I was glued to it from the very first page, and here I will quote it:<br/><br/><i>WE<br/>When it is over, We breathe and ache like old oak, lik</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8084516572709046273" style="display:none">Holy crap. Ladies and gentlemen, Lisa McMann has done it once again. This book was similar to the Dream Catcher trilogy (Wake, Fade and Gone) yet so different. Cryer's Cross totally brought the words 'eerie' and 'haunting' to a whole new level, well maybe not, but its sure damn close! It had me shuddering throughout but I couldn't bring myself to tear away from the pages, I was glued to it from the very first page, and here I will quote it:<br /><br /><i>WE<br />When it is over, We breathe and ache like old oak, like peeling birch. One of Our lost souls set free. We move, a chess piece in the dark room, cast-iron legs a centimetre at a time, crying out in silent carved graffiti. Calling to Our next victim, Our next savior. We carve on Our face:<br />TOUCH ME<br />SAVE MY SOUL</i><br /><br />If that didn't already give you the heebie jeebies then I don't know what will. How creepy is that huh? (The rest of the book isn't written like that by the way, in case you were wondering) That first paragraph had me captivated and that did it for me, I was totally addicted and desperate to finish it and finding out the haunting mystery behind it all. The plot was so uniquely special and different and it will take you on a ride that will leave you breathless, tormented and on the edge of your seat. An unsolved mystery, buried secrets and a truly scary haunt all mixed up in this one-of-a-kind novel.<br /><br />&lt;**SPOILER ALERT**&gt;<br />Kendall is in her senior year and she suffers from OCD. She has a sweet and sufferingly-ordinary boyfriend who cares and loves her. The small town she lives in has been shaken to its roots by a girl who has recently gone missing and this has Kendall freaked. Enter two new kids, a girl and her brother, Jacien (Hah-see-ahn) who acts like a total jerk to basically everyone around him, Kendall not excluded. When the fire around the missing girl has finally died down, another tragedy strikes, and this time, its aimed at Kendall's boyfriend, Nico, who's been acting really weird ever since the first week of school, drowsy, totally out of it, like he's in another world. When he's the next victim to go missing, Kendall is grief-stricken and scared out of her wits. This is when she starts getting closer to Jacien, sort of. Jacien is a pretty moody, depressed, angst guy who's throwing a nasty temper at having been forced into moving to the middle-of-nowhere-Cryer's Cross. He's the distraction for Kendall and he starts to thaw a bit while hanging out with her, which I was totally for, and I so love the fact that he takes in her OCD without any problems whatsoever because he understands what she goes through, though he doesn't suffer from it, and he's totally casual with it. I totally lol'd at a part where Kendall's straightening desks and when she comes to his, he's like all "Go ahead" xD love him in that scene...I was basically urging them on when they grew closer and stuff and my favourite part was the party scene *sigh*<br /><br />Anyway, this book totally had me eating out of the palm of its hand, fans of Lisa McMann should DEFINITELY pick this up, heck, anyone who loves a good, spine-tingling novel should pick this up! I am SO for this book being made into a movie, I can totally see it...once again, Lisa, a hell of an awesome job well done :D:D:D</span>
  <a data-text-id="8084516572709046273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pzWTYF29iDJuA+FKAHUkk2/c3m4ixwocladizRb1QiXAG/gDmteHT4RSKzA4STPnuyTQ4LXhcDd4Y3TSperGvA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lblphFO4X4nlt4CDW+BNjYXMLQqSCdmWQ8IxwFAL1rbylwLnlNJQ9A/mSvlj3Fr5UTQjhAUvo72uBiff4xRSLw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer1027714066023808136">Lisa McMann lives and writes in the Phoenix area. Her books include the NYT bestselling THE UNWANTEDS series (the new UNWANTEDS QUESTS series begins Feb 7, 2017) and the YA paranormal WAKE trilogy. Other books include the VISIONS trilogy, CRYER'S CROSS, DEAD TO YOU, INFINITY RING: The Trap Door, and the GOING WILD trilogy (book 2 coming autumn 2017).<br/><br/>You can find more info at Lisa'a website, <a href='http://lisamcmann.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>lisamc</a></span>
  <span id="freeText1027714066023808136" style="display:none">Lisa McMann lives and writes in the Phoenix area. This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
